<p style="margin:0pt 1.8pt .0001pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Notes to Condensed
Consolidated Financial Statements</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 1.8pt .0001pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">June 30, 2007</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 1.8pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(Unaudited)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 1.8pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 1 &#151; Basis of
Presentation</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 9.9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The accompanying
unaudited, condensed consolidated financial statements have been prepared
pursuant to rules and regulations of the Securities and Exchange Commission
and, therefore, do not include all information and footnote disclosures
normally included in audited financial statements.&#160; However, in the opinion of management, all
adjustments (which include only normal adjustments) necessary to present fairly
the results of operations, financial position and cash flows have been
made.&#160; It is suggested that these
statements be read in conjunction with the financial statements included in
Abbott&#146;s Annual Report on Form 10-K for the year ended December 31, 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 2 &#151; Assets and Liabilities Classified as Held for
Sale</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On July 11, 2007, Abbott
announced that Abbott and GE mutually agreed to terminate the previously
announced contract to sell Abbott&#146;s core laboratory diagnostics business,
including Abbott Point of Care, to GE.&#160;
The assets of the operations held for sale and the liabilities to be
assumed in the intended sale have been classified as held for sale in the
Condensed Consolidated Balance Sheet as of June 30, 2007.&#160; These assets and liabilities will no longer
be classified as held for sale beginning in the third quarter of 2007.&#160; Prior years&#146; balance sheets have not been
adjusted.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Effective
on the date that Abbott agreed to sell its core laboratory diagnostics
businesses to GE, depreciation of property and equipment and amortization of
intangible assets was discontinued.&#160;
Accordingly, the consolidated results of operations for the six months
ended June 30, 2006, include six months of depreciation and amortization and
the consolidated results of operations for the six months ended June 30, 2007,
include depreciation and amortization through January 17, 2007.&#160;&#160; The amount of depreciation and amortization
that was discontinued amounted to approximately $99 million for the six months
ended June 30, 2007.&#160; This depreciation
and amortization will be recorded in the third quarter of 2007 as these
operations will no longer be classified as held for sale.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt .0001pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The assets and
liabilities classified as held for sale as of June 30, 2007, consist of the
following:</font></p>

(Unaudited), continued</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 3 &#151; Adoption of New Accounting Standards</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Effective
January 1, 2007, Abbott adopted Statement of Financial Accounting Standards
(SFAS) No. 157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements,&#148; SFAS No. 159, &#147;The Fair Value Option
for Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities,&#148; and FASB Interpretation No.
48, &#147;Accounting for Uncertainty in Income Taxes.&#148;&#160;&#160; Adoption of these Standards and
Interpretation did not have a material impact on Abbott&#146;s financial position.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SFAS No. 157 applies to
all fair measurements not otherwise specified in an existing standard, it
clarifies how to measure fair value, and it expands fair value
disclosures.&#160; For Abbott, SFAS No. 157
does not significantly change the valuation of assets versus previous practice.&#160; However, for liabilities, SFAS No. 157
requires that a fair value measurement be the amount that a company would pay
to transfer a liability to a third party.&#160;
Under previous practice, liabilities were valued under a number of
different methods.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SFAS No. 159 allows
companies to measure specific financial assets and liabilities at fair value,
such as debt or equity investments.&#160;&#160; The
fair value option for the investment in Boston Scientific common stock was
applied effective January 1, 2007.&#160;
Abbott applied the fair value option to its investment in Boston
Scientific stock under SFAS No. 159 because, unlike its other equity
investments, the Boston Scientific stock is not a strategic investment and
Abbott is required to dispose of the stock no later than October 2008.&#160; Abbott remains subject to a limitation on the
amount of shares it may sell in any one month through October 2007 and Abbott
will not reacquire the Boston Scientific shares it sells.&#160; Accordingly, since at adoption, realized
gains or losses were expected in the near future, the fair value option better
represented the near-term expected earnings impact from sales of the
stock.&#160;&#160; Under the fair value option, any
cumulative unrealized gains or losses on an equity investment previously
accounted for as an available-for-sale security is recorded as a cumulative
effect adjustment to retained earnings as of the date of adoption of the
standard.&#160; The pretax and after tax
adjustment to Earnings employed in the business upon adoption was $297 million
and $189 million, respectively, and the fair value and carrying amount of the
investment before and after adoption was $1.0 billion.&#160; The pretax and after tax adjustment to
Accumulated other comprehensive income was $303 million and $182 million,
respectively.&#160;&#160; The effect of the
adoption on deferred income taxes was not significant.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">FASB Interpretation No. 48 requires that a recorded
tax benefit must be more likely than not of being sustained upon examination by
tax authorities based upon its technical merits. The amount of benefit recorded
is the largest amount of benefit that is greater than 50 percent likely of
being realized upon ultimate settlement.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 4 &#151; Business Combinations and Related
Transactions</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On April 21, 2006,
Abbott acquired Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and endovascular solutions
businesses for approximately $4.1 billion, in cash, in connection with Boston
Scientific&#146;s acquisition of Guidant.&#160; In
addition, Abbott will also pay to Boston Scientific $250 million each upon
government approvals to market the <i>Xience</i>
<i>V </i>drug-eluting stent in the U.S.
and in Japan.&#160; Each $250 million payment
will result in additional consideration for the acquisition of Guidant&#146;s
vascular intervention and endovascular solutions businesses.&#160; The allocation of the purchase price as of
June 30, 2006 resulted in a charge of $452 million in the second quarter of
2006 for acquired in-process research and development, intangible assets of
$1.2 billion, goodwill (primarily deductible) of $1.8 billion and tangible net
assets of $620 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
substantial amount of the acquired in-process research and development charge
relating to the Guidant acquisition related to drug eluting and bioabsorbable
stents.&#160; The research efforts ranged from
35 percent to 85 percent complete at the date of acquisition.&#160; The valuation method used to fair value the
projects was the Multi-period Excess Earnings Method (Income Approach) and the
risk-adjusted discount rates used ranged from 16 percent to 25 percent.&#160; In developing assumptions for the valuation
model, comparable Abbott products or products marketed by competitors were used
to estimate pricing, margins and expense levels.&#160; As of June 30, 2007, the research efforts
were primarily on schedule.&#160; The
estimated projected costs to complete totaled approximately $520 million as of
June 30, 2007, with anticipated product launch dates from 2008 through
2013.&#160; There have been no significant
changes in the development plans for the acquired incomplete projects.&#160; Significant net cash inflows will commence
within one to two years after product launch.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='6',FILE='C:\fc\211212815126_D11189_2292149\18715-1-de.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Jul 30 21:28 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Notes to Condensed
Consolidated Financial Statements<br>
June 30, 2007<br>
(Unaudited), continued</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In order to
facilitate Boston Scientific&#146;s acquisition of Guidant, Abbott also acquired
64.6 million shares of Boston Scientific common stock directly from Boston
Scientific and loaned $900 million to a wholly-owned subsidiary of Boston
Scientific.&#160; The common stock was valued
at $1.3 billion and the note receivable was valued at $829 million at the
acquisition date.&#160; In connection with the
acquisition of the shares, Boston Scientific is entitled to certain after-tax
gains upon Abbott&#146;s sale of the shares.&#160;
In addition, Boston Scientific agreed to reimburse Abbott for certain
borrowing costs on debt incurred to acquire the Boston Scientific shares.
Abbott recorded a net derivative financial instruments liability of $59 million
for the gain-sharing derivative financial instrument liability and the interest
derivative financial instrument asset.&#160; The
effect of recording the shares, the loan to Boston Scientific and the
derivative financial instruments at fair value on the date of acquisition
resulted in the recording of additional goodwill of approximately $204 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In December 2006, Abbott acquired Kos Pharmaceuticals
Inc. for cash of approximately $3.8 billion, net of cash held by Kos
Pharmaceuticals Inc.&#160; The valuation of
certain tangible assets and liabilities related to the acquisition of Kos
Pharmaceuticals Inc. is preliminary.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
charge of approximately $1.3 billion for acquired in-process research and
development was recorded relating to the Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. acquisition,
which related primarily to cholesterol treatment drugs.&#160; The research efforts ranged from 70 percent
to 80 percent complete at the date of acquisition. &#160;The valuation method used to fair value the
projects was the Multi-period Excess Earnings Method (Income Approach) and the
risk-adjusted discount rate used was 16 percent.&#160; In developing assumptions for the valuation
model, comparable Abbott products or products marketed by competitors were used
to estimate pricing, margins and expense levels.&#160; As of June 30, 2007, one drug was approved
for marketing in the U.S. and the remaining research efforts were primarily on
schedule.&#160; The estimated projected costs
to complete the projects totaled approximately $71 million as of June 30, 2007
with anticipated product launches in 2008.&#160;
There have been no significant changes in the development plans for the
acquired incomplete projects.&#160;
Significant net cash inflows will commence with the launches of the
products.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 5 &#151; Supplemental Financial Information</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Other (income) expense, net for the second quarter of
2007 includes a $48 million fair market value gain adjustment to Abbott&#146;s
investment in Boston Scientific common stock and a realized gain of $37 million
on the sales of Boston Scientific stock.&#160;
Other (income) expense, net for the first six months of 2007 includes a
$101 million fair market value loss adjustment to Abbott&#146;s investment in Boston
Scientific common stock and a realized gain of $37 million on the sales of
Boston Scientific stock.&#160; Other (income)
expense, net for the second quarter and first six months of 2006 includes fair
value gain adjustments of $75 million to certain derivative financial
instruments included with the investment in Boston Scientific common stock.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 6 &#151; Taxes on
Earnings</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on earnings reflect
the estimated annual effective rates and include charges for interest and
penalties.&#160; The effective tax rate for
the six months ended June 30, 2006 includes the effect of discrete tax events
that occurred in the second quarter of 2006.&#160;
For the six months ended June 30, 2006, 6.2 percentage points of tax
benefit was attributed to discrete items, primarily the tax benefit on acquired
in-process and collaborations research and development.&#160; The effective tax rates are less than the
statutory U.S. federal income tax rate principally due to the domestic dividend
exclusion and the benefit of lower statutory tax rates and tax exemptions in
several taxing jurisdictions.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Unrecognized tax benefits
as of the adoption of FASB Interpretation No. 48 on January 1, 2007 were
approximately $579 million, which if recognized, would decrease taxes on
earnings.&#160; The total amount of
unrecognized tax benefits that, if recognized, would affect the effective tax
rate in 2007 totaled approximately <b>$</b>143
million.&#160; Abbott does not expect the
total amount of unrecognized tax benefits as of June 30, 2007, to change
significantly within the next twelve months.&#160;
Reserves for interest and penalties are not significant.&#160; In the U.S., Abbott&#146;s federal income tax
returns through 2003 are settled, and the income tax returns for years after
2003 are open.&#160; There are numerous other
income tax jurisdictions for which tax returns are not yet settled, none of
which are individually significant.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 62.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 7 &#151; Litigation
and Environmental Matters</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott has been identified as a potentially
responsible party for investigation and cleanup costs at a number of locations
in the United States and Puerto Rico under federal and state remediation laws
and is investigating potential contamination at a number of company-owned
locations.&#160; Abbott has recorded an
estimated cleanup cost for each site for which management believes Abbott has a
probable loss exposure.&#160; No individual
site cleanup exposure is expected to exceed $3&nbsp;million, and the aggregate
cleanup exposure is not expected to exceed $15&nbsp;million.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">There are
two patent disputes with third parties who claim Abbott&#146;s products infringe
their patents.&nbsp; In the first dispute, which Abbott assumed as part of the
Guidant acquisition, reserves equal to the expected resolution have been
recorded.&#160; In the second dispute, filed
in April 2007, Abbott is unable to estimate a range of possible loss, if any,
and no reserve has been recorded.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">There are several civil actions pending
brought by individuals or entities that allege generally that Abbott and
numerous pharmaceutical companies reported false or misleading pricing
information relating to the average wholesale price of certain pharmaceutical
products in connection with federal, state and private reimbursement.&#160; Civil actions have also been brought against
Abbott, and in some cases other members of the pharmaceutical industry, by
state attorneys general seeking to recover alleged damages on behalf of state
Medicaid programs.&#160; In May 2006, Abbott
was notified that the U.S. Department of Justice intervened in a civil
whistle-blower lawsuit alleging that Abbott inflated prices for Medicaid and
Medicare reimbursable drugs.&#160; The outcome
of these investigations and litigation could include the imposition of fines or
penalties.&#160; Abbott is unable to estimate
the amount of possible loss, and no loss reserves have been recorded for these
exposures.&#160; Many of the products involved
in these cases are Hospira products.&#160;
Hospira, Abbott&#146;s former hospital products business, was spun off to
Abbott&#146;s shareholders in 2004.&#160; Abbott
retained liability for losses that result from these cases and investigations
to the extent any such losses both relate to the sale of Hospira&#146;s products
prior to the spin-off of Hospira and relate to allegations that were made in
such pending and future cases and investigations that were the same as
allegations existing at the date of the spin-off.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Within the next year, legal proceedings may
occur that may result in a change in the estimated reserves recorded by
Abbott.&nbsp; For its legal proceedings and environmental exposures, except as
noted in the second and third paragraphs of this footnote, Abbott estimates the
range of possible loss to be from approximately $160 million to $290 million.&#160; The recorded reserve balance at June 30, 2007
for these proceedings and exposures was approximately $190 million.&nbsp; These
reserves represent management&#146;s best estimate of probable loss, as defined by
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;5, &#147;Accounting for
Contingencies.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While it is not feasible to predict the outcome of all
such proceedings and exposures with certainty, management believes that their
ultimate disposition should not have a material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s
financial position, cash flows, or results of operations, except for the cases
and investigations discussed in the third paragraph of this footnote, the
resolution of which could be material to cash flows or results of operations
for a quarter.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott funds its domestic defined benefit
plans according to IRS funding limitations.&#160;
In the first quarters of 2007 and 2006, $200 was contributed to the main
domestic defined benefit plan and $75 and $40, respectively, was contributed to
the post-employment medical and dental benefit plans.</font></p>

  <p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:right;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">18,253</font></p>
  </td>
  <td width="0%" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:.82%;">

<p style="margin:0pt 45.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 10 &#151; Segment Information</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt .7pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Revenue
Segments </font></i>&#151; Abbott&#146;s principal business is the discovery,
development, manufacture and sale of a broad line of health care products.&#160; Abbott&#146;s products are generally sold directly
to retailers, wholesalers, hospitals, health care facilities, laboratories,
physicians&#146; offices and government agencies throughout the world.&#160; Abbott&#146;s reportable segments are as follows:</p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='9',FILE='C:\fc\211212815126_D11189_2292149\18715-1-de.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Jul 30 21:28 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Notes to Condensed
Consolidated Financial Statements<br>
June 30, 2007<br>
(Unaudited), continued</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Pharmaceutical
Products</font></i> &#151; Worldwide sales of a broad line of
pharmaceuticals.&#160; For segment reporting
purposes, two pharmaceutical divisions are aggregated and reported as the
Pharmaceutical Products segment.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Nutritional
Products</font></i><font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;"> &#151; </font>Worldwide
sales of a broad line of adult and pediatric nutritional products.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Diagnostic Products</font></i><font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;"> &#151; </font>Worldwide sales of diagnostic systems
and tests for blood banks, hospitals, commercial laboratories and
alternate-care testing sites.&#160; For
segment reporting purposes, three diagnostic divisions are aggregated and reported
as the Diagnostic Products segment.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Vascular</font></i>
<i>Products</i><font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;">&nbsp;&#151; </font>Worldwide sales of coronary, endovascular and vessel
closure products.</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s underlying
accounting records are maintained on a legal entity basis for government and
public reporting requirements.&#160; Segment
disclosures are on a performance basis consistent with internal management
reporting.&#160; Intersegment transfers of
inventory are recorded at standard cost and are not a measure of segment
operating earnings.&#160; The cost of some
corporate functions and the cost of certain employee benefits are charged to
segments at predetermined rates that approximate cost.&#160; Remaining costs, if any, are not allocated to
segments<b>.&#160;
</b>Effective in the second quarter of 2007, the Diagnostic
segment was reorganized.&#160; Prior period
segment information has been adjusted to reflect this change.&#160; For acquisitions prior to 2006, substantially
all intangible assets and related amortization are not allocated to segments.<b>&#160; </b>The
following segment information has been prepared in accordance with the internal
accounting policies of Abbott, as described above, and are not presented in
accordance with generally accepted accounting principles applied to the
consolidated financial statements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 17.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><hr size="1" width="160" noshade color="black" align="left" style="width:120.0pt;"></div>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The decrease in
Nutritional Products segment sales and operating earnings for the six months
ended June 30, 2007 was due to the completion of the U.S. co-promotion of <i>Synagis</i> in 2006.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The increase in Vascular
Product segment sales for the six months ended June 30, 2007, is primarily due
to the acquisition of Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and endovascular
solutions businesses on April 21, 2006.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(c)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Sales from the diabetes,
bulk pharmaceuticals, spine and animal health businesses are included in Other
sales.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(d)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Approximately 40 to 45
percent of the annual cost of share-based awards will typically be recognized
in the first quarter due to the timing of the granting of share-based awards.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(e)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Other, net for the three
months and six months ended June 30, 2007, includes acquisition integration
expenses related to the acquisitions of Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and
endovascular solutions businesses and Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. and the reversal
of depreciation on property and equipment classified as held for sale that was
recorded by the Diagnostics segment.</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 11 &#151; Incentive Stock
Programs</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 1.45pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">In the first six months of 2007,
Abbott granted 17,481,056 stock options, 12,594,154 replacement stock options,
1,503,100 (net of forfeitures of 37,400 shares) restricted stock awards and
549,230 restricted stock units under the programs.&#160; At June 30, 2007, approximately 30&nbsp;million
shares were reserved for future grants.&#160;
Information regarding the number of options outstanding and exercisable
at June 30, 2007 is as follows:</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 45.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">The total unrecognized compensation cost related to all share-based
compensation plans at June 30, 2007, amounted to approximately $364 million
which is expected to be recognized over the next three years.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">Note&nbsp;13&nbsp;</font>&#151;<font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;"> Goodwill and Intangible
Assets</font></font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">Foreign currency translation adjustments and other
adjustments increased goodwill in the first six months of 2007 and 2006 by
approximately $129<b>  </b>and $394,
respectively.&#160; Abbott recorded total
goodwill of approximately $2,011 related to the acquisition of </font><font face="Times New Roman">Guidant&#146;s
vascular intervention and endovascular solutions businesses<font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;"> in the second quarter of 2006.&#160; There were no reductions of goodwill relating
to impairments or disposal of all or a portion of a business.&#160; </font>The amount of goodwill related to
reportable segments at June 30, 2007 was $5,334 for the Pharmaceutical Products
segment, $353 for the Nutritional Products segment, $322 for the Diagnostics Products
segment and $1,958 for the Vascular Products segment.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">The gross amount of amortizable intangible assets,
primarily product rights and technology was $9,022<b>  </b>as of June 30, 2007 and $8,988 as of December&nbsp;31, 2006,
and accumulated amortization was $2,991 as of June 30, 2007 and $2,602 as of
December 31, 2006.&#160; The estimated annual
amortization expense for intangible assets is $764<b>  </b>in 2007, $688 in 2008, $691 in 2009, $692 in 2010 and $672 in
2011.&#160; Intangible assets are amortized
primarily on a straight-line basis over 1 to 25&nbsp;years (average
11&nbsp;years).</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">11</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<p style="margin:0pt 36.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Notes to Condensed
Consolidated Financial Statements<br>
June 30, 2007<br>
(Unaudited), continued</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 36.0pt .0001pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Note 14 &#151;
Restructuring Plans</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;letter-spacing:-.1pt;">(dollars in millions)</font></i></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2007, 2006 and 2005, Abbott management approved plans to realign its worldwide
pharmaceutical manufacturing operations and selected domestic and international
commercial and research and development operations in order to reduce
costs.&#160; Additional charges of $67 and $22
were subsequently recorded in the first six months of 2007 and 2006,
respectively, relating to these restructurings, primarily for accelerated
depreciation.&#160; In addition, Abbott
implemented facilities restructuring plans in the second quarter of 2007
related to the acquired operations of Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc., which resulted
in an increase to goodwill of approximately $52.&#160; The following summarizes the activity for
restructurings:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div align="center" style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

 <tr style="page-break-inside:avoid;">
  <td width="451" valign="bottom" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:337.95pt;">
  <p style="font-size:8.0pt;font-weight:bold;line-height:8.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><!-- SET mrlHTMLTableCenter --></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="line-height:normal;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For assets and liabilities that are measured using quoted prices in
active markets, the total fair value is the published market price per unit
multiplied by the number of units held without consideration of transaction
costs.&#160; Assets and liabilities that are
measured using significant other observable inputs are valued by reference to
similar assets or liabilities, adjusted for contract restrictions and other
terms specific to that asset or liability.&#160;
For these items, a significant portion of fair value is derived by
reference to quoted prices of similar assets or liabilities in active markets.&#160; For all remaining assets and liabilities,
fair value is derived using a fair value model, such as a discounted cash flow
model or Black-Scholes model.</font></p>

<div style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><hr size="1" width="160" noshade color="black" align="left" style="width:120.0pt;"></div>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 20.0pt;text-indent:-20.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:7.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="1" style="font-size:7.0pt;">The Pharmaceutical Products
segment had an agreement with Boehringer Ingelheim (BI) to co-promote and distribute
three of its products in the U.S.&#160; In
2005, Abbott and BI amended the agreement and effective January&nbsp;1, 2006,
Abbott no longer distributed or recorded sales for distribution activities for
the BI products, although Abbott recorded a small amount of co-promotion
revenue in the first quarter of 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Worldwide sales
for the second quarter and six months 2007 compared to 2006 reflects the
acquisitions of Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and endovascular solutions
businesses on April 21, 2006 and Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. in the fourth quarter
of 2006. The sales growth in 2007 also reflects unit growth and the positive
effect of the relatively weaker U.S. dollar.&#160;
The relatively weaker U.S. dollar increased second quarter 2007
consolidated net sales by 2.7 percent, Total International sales by 5.3
percent, Pharmaceutical Products segment sales by 2.7 percent and Diagnostic
Products segment sales by 3.8 percent over the second quarter of 2006.&#160; The relatively weaker U.S. dollar also
increased the first six months 2007 consolidated net sales by 2.7 percent,
Total International sales by 5.4 percent, Pharmaceutical Products segment sales
by 2.7 percent and Diagnostic Products segment sales by 3.9 percent over the
first six months of 2006.&#160; The sales
growth for the second quarter and six months 2006 compared to 2005, excluding
sales of BI products, reflects the acquisition of Guidant&#146;s vascular
intervention and endovascular solutions businesses on April 21, 2006. The sales
growth in 2006 also reflects unit growth, partially offset by the negative
effect of the relatively stronger U.S. dollar.&#160;
The relatively stronger U.S. dollar decreased second quarter 2006
consolidated net sales by 0.9 percent, Total International sales by 2.0
percent, Pharmaceutical Products segment sales by 0.9 percent and&#160; Diagnostic Products segment sales by 1.9
percent over the second quarter of 2005. The relatively stronger U.S. dollar
also decreased the first six months 2006 consolidated net sales by 1.8 percent,
Total International sales by 3.9 percent, Pharmaceutical Products segment sales
by 1.9 percent and Diagnostic Products segment sales by 3.2 percent over the
first six months of 2005.&#160; Sales growth
in 2007 for the Nutritional Products segment was unfavorably impacted by the
completion of the U.S. co-promotion of <i>Synagis
</i>in 2006.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">14</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<p style="line-height:1.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Increased sales of <i>HUMIRA</i>
and <i>Depakote</i> accounted for the
majority of the sales increase for U.S. Specialty products in both 2007 and
2006.&#160; U.S. sales of <i>HUMIRA</i> were $696 million, $501 million and
$353 million for the six months ended June 30, 2007, 2006 and 2005,
respectively.&#160; U.S. Primary Care sales in
2007 were favorably impacted by sales of <i>Niaspan</i>,
a new product from the acquisition of Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. in the fourth
quarter of 2006.&#160; U.S. Primary Care sales
were also favorably impacted by increased sales of <i>TriCor</i> in both periods and were unfavorably impacted by
decreased sales of <i>Omnicef</i> in
2007 and <i>Biaxin</i> in 2007 and 2006
due to the introduction of generic competition.&#160;
Sales of <i>Omnicef</i> were $203
million and $244 million for the six months ended June 30, 2007 and 2006,
respectively, and sales of <i>Biaxin</i>
were $12 million, $80 million and $173 million for the six months ended June
30, 2007, 2006 and 2005, respectively.&#160;&#160;
Increased sales of <i>HUMIRA</i>
favorably impacted International Pharmaceutical sales in 2007 and 2006.&#160; International sales of <i>HUMIRA</i> were $611 million, $382 million and
$250 million for the six months ended June 30, 2007, 2006 and 2005,
respectively.&#160; The relatively weaker U.S.
dollar increased International Pharmaceutical sales by 5.6 percent in 2007 and
the relatively stronger U.S. dollar decreased International Pharmaceutical
sales by 4.5 percent in 2006.&#160; The
decrease in sales of U.S. Pediatric Nutritional sales in 2006 was due to
overall infant nutritionals non-WIC category decline and competitive share
loss.&#160; International Pediatric
Nutritionals sales increases in 2007 and 2006 were due primarily to volume
growth in developing countries.&#160; The
relatively weaker U.S. dollar increased Immunochemistry sales by 4.2 percent in
2007 and the relatively stronger U.S. dollar decreased Immunochemistry sales by
3.5 percent in 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The gross profit
margin was 56.0 percent for the
second quarter 2007, compared to 56.6 percent for the second quarter 2006.&#160; First six months 2007 gross profit margin was
56.2 percent, compared to 57.3 percent for the first six months 2006.&#160; The decreases in the gross profit margins in
2007 were due, in part, to the effect of the unfavorable impact in 2007 from
the completion of the U.S. co-promotion of <i>Synagis</i>
in 2006 as well as generic competition for <i>Omnicef</i>
and <i>Biaxin</i> sales in 2007.&#160; Increased amortization of intangible assets
acquired in 2006 also had an unfavorable impact on the gross profit margins in
2007.&#160; Suspended depreciation for the
operations classified as held for sale favorably impacted the gross profit
margins in both periods of 2007.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Research and
development expenses increased 4.9
percent in the second quarter 2007 and 15.5
percent for the first six months 2007 over comparable 2006 periods.&#160; These increases reflect the effect of the
acquisitions of Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and endovascular solutions
businesses on April 21, 2006 and Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. in the fourth quarter
of 2006.&#160; These increases also reflect
increased spending to support pipeline programs, including follow-on
indications for <i>HUMIRA,</i> and
ABT-335, ABT-874, controlled-release <i>Vicodin
</i>and <i>Xience V</i>.&#160; The majority of research and development
expenditures is concentrated on pharmaceutical products.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">15</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='15',FILE='C:\fc\21121323747_D11189_2292149\18715-1-dg.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Jul 30 21:32 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="margin:0pt 36.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">FINANCIAL REVIEW<br>
(continued)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Selling, general
and administrative expenses for the second quarter and first six months 2007
increased 18.2 percent and 20.1 percent, respectively, over the
comparable 2006 periods.&#160;&#160; These
increases reflect the effect of the acquisitions of Guidant&#146;s vascular
intervention and endovascular solutions businesses on April 21, 2006 and Kos
Pharmaceuticals Inc. in the fourth quarter of 2006.&#160; The increases also reflect increased selling
and marketing support for new and existing products, including continued
spending for <i>HUMIRA </i>and the
continuing international launch of <i>Xience V</i>,
as well as spending on other marketed pharmaceutical products.&#160; In
the third quarter of 2007, Abbott terminated a contract that will result in a
third quarter non-recurring charge of approximately $94 million, net of income
taxes.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Assets and
Liabilities Classified as Held for Sale</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On July 11, 2007, Abbott
announced that Abbott and GE mutually agreed to terminate the previously
announced contract to sell Abbott&#146;s core laboratory diagnostics business,
including Abbott Point of Care, to GE.&#160;
The assets of the operations held for sale and the liabilities to be
assumed in the intended sale have been classified as held for sale in the
Condensed Consolidated Balance Sheet as of June 30, 2007.&#160; These assets and liabilities will no longer
be classified as held for sale beginning in the third quarter of 2007.&#160; Prior years&#146; balance sheets have not been
adjusted.</font></p>

<p style="color:black;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;punctuation-wrap:simple;vertical-align:baseline;"><font size="2" color="black" face="Times New Roman" style="color:windowtext;font-size:10.0pt;">Effective
on the date that Abbott agreed to sell its core laboratory diagnostics
businesses to GE, depreciation of property and equipment and amortization of
intangible assets was discontinued.&#160;
Accordingly, the consolidated results of operations for the six months ended
June 30, 2006, include six months of depreciation and amortization and the
consolidated results of operations for the six months ended June 30, 2007,
include depreciation and amortization through January 17, 2007.&#160;&#160; The amount of depreciation and amortization
that was discontinued amounted to approximately $99 million for the six months
ended June 30, 2007.&#160; This depreciation
and amortization will be recorded in the third quarter of 2007, as these
operations will no longer be classified as held for sale.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt .0001pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The assets and
liabilities classified as held for sale as of June 30, 2007, consist of the
following:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">(dollars in thousands)</font></i></p>

<div align="center" style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="border-collapse:collapse;">
 <tr bgcolor="#CCEEFF" style="page-break-inside:avoid;">
  <td width="351" valign="top" style="padding:0pt .7pt 0pt 0pt;width:263.4pt;">
  <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><!-- SET mrlHTMLTableCenter -->Trade accounts receivable,
  net</p>

<p style="line-height:1.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt .0001pt 0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Restructurings</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(<i>dollars in millions</i>)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2007, 2006 and 2005, Abbott management approved plans to realign its worldwide
pharmaceutical manufacturing operations and selected domestic and international
commercial and research and development operations in order to reduce costs.&#160; Additional charges of $67 and $22 were
subsequently recorded in the first six months of 2007 and 2006, respectively,
relating to these restructurings, primarily for accelerated depreciation.&#160; In addition, Abbott implemented facilities
restructuring plans in the second quarter of 2007 related to the acquired
operations of Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc., which resulted in an increase to
goodwill of approximately $52.&#160; The
following summarizes the activity for restructurings:</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 36.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">FINANCIAL REVIEW<br>
(continued)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Business Combinations and
Related Transactions</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On April 21, 2006,
Abbott acquired Guidant&#146;s vascular intervention and endovascular solutions
businesses for approximately $4.1 billion, in cash, in connection with Boston
Scientific&#146;s acquisition of Guidant.&#160; In
addition, Abbott will also pay to Boston Scientific $250 million each upon
government approvals to market the <i>Xience</i>
<i>V </i>drug-eluting stent in the U.S.
and in Japan.&#160; Each $250 million payment
will result in additional consideration for the acquisition of Guidant&#146;s
vascular intervention and endovascular solutions businesses.&#160; The allocation of the purchase price as of
June 30, 2006 resulted in a charge of $452 million in the second quarter of
2006 for acquired in-process research and development, intangible assets of
$1.2 billion, goodwill (primarily deductible) of $1.8 billion and tangible net
assets of $620 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
substantial amount of the acquired in-process research and development charge
relating to the Guidant acquisition related to drug eluting and bioabsorbable
stents.&#160; The research efforts ranged from
35 percent to 85 percent complete at the date of acquisition.&#160; The valuation method used to fair value the
projects was the Multi-period Excess Earnings Method (Income Approach) and the
risk-adjusted discount rates used ranged from 16 percent to 25 percent.&#160; In developing assumptions for the valuation
model, comparable Abbott products or products marketed by competitors were used
to estimate pricing, margins and expense levels.&#160; As of June 30, 2007, the research efforts
were primarily on schedule.&#160; The
estimated projected costs to complete totaled approximately $520 million as of
June 30, 2007, with anticipated product launch dates from 2008 through
2013.&#160; There have been no significant
changes in the development plans for the acquired incomplete projects.&#160; Significant net cash inflows will commence
within one to two years after product launch.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 14.4pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In order to
facilitate Boston Scientific&#146;s acquisition of Guidant, Abbott also acquired
64.6 million shares of Boston Scientific common stock directly from Boston
Scientific and loaned $900 million to a wholly-owned subsidiary of Boston
Scientific.&#160; The common stock was valued
at $1.3 billion and the note receivable was valued at $829 million at the
acquisition date.&#160; In connection with the
acquisition of the shares, Boston Scientific is entitled to certain after-tax
gains upon Abbott&#146;s sale of the shares.&#160;
In addition, Boston Scientific agreed to reimburse Abbott for certain
borrowing costs on debt incurred to acquire the Boston Scientific shares.&#160;&#160; Abbott recorded a net derivative financial
instruments liability of $59 million for the gain-sharing derivative financial
instrument liability and the interest derivative financial instrument
asset.&#160; The effect of recording the
shares, the loan to Boston Scientific and the derivative financial instruments
at fair value on the date of acquisition resulted in the recording of
additional goodwill of approximately $204 million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In December 2006, Abbott acquired Kos Pharmaceuticals
Inc. for cash of approximately $3.8 billion, net of cash held by Kos
Pharmaceuticals Inc.&#160; The valuation of
certain tangible assets and liabilities related to the acquisition of Kos
Pharmaceuticals Inc. are preliminary.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
charge of approximately $1.3 billion for acquired in-process research and
development was recorded relating to the Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. acquisition,
which related primarily to cholesterol treatment drugs.&#160; The research efforts ranged from 70 percent
to 80 percent complete at the date of acquisition.&#160; The valuation method used to fair value the
projects was the Multi-period Excess Earnings Method (Income Approach) and the
risk-adjusted discount rate used was 16 percent.&#160; In developing assumptions for the valuation
model, comparable Abbott products or products marketed by competitors were used
to estimate pricing, margins and expense levels.&#160; As of June 30, 2007, one drug was approved
for marketing in the U.S. and the remaining research efforts were primarily on
schedule.&#160; The estimated projected costs
to complete the projects totaled approximately $71 million as of June 30, 2007
with anticipated product launches in 2008.&#160;
There have been no significant changes in the development plans for the
acquired incomplete projects.&#160;
Significant net cash inflows will commence with the launches of the
products.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 44.3pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Interest expense</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Interest expense
increased in the second quarter and first six months of 2007 due primarily to
higher borrowings as a result of the acquisitions of Guidant&#146;s vascular
intervention and endovascular solutions businesses and Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc.
and Abbott&#146;s investment in the Boston Scientific common stock and note
receivable.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<p style="margin:0pt 36.0pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">FINANCIAL REVIEW<br>
(continued)</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(Income) from TAP
Pharmaceutical Products Inc. Joint Venture</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s income
from the TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc. joint venture is higher in the first
six months of 2007 compared to 2006 due primarily to a favorable outcome in a
patent dispute recorded by TAP Pharmaceutical Products Inc. in the first
quarter of 2007.&#160; In addition, the second
quarter of 2006 was favorably impacted by the sales of certain product rights.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Other (income) expense,
net</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Other (income)
expense, net for the second quarter of 2007 includes a $48 million fair market
value gain adjustment to Abbott&#146;s investment in Boston Scientific common stock
and a realized gain of $37 million on the sales of Boston Scientific stock. &#160;Other (income) expense, net for the first six
months of 2007 includes a $101 million fair market value loss adjustment to
Abbott&#146;s investment in Boston Scientific common stock and a realized gain of
$37 million on the sales of Boston Scientific stock.&#160; Other (income) expense, net for the second
quarter and first six months of 2006 includes fair value gain adjustments of
$75 million to certain derivative financial instruments included with the
investment in Boston Scientific common stock.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Effective January 1,
2007, Abbott adopted Statement of Financial Accounting Standards (SFAS) No.
157, &#147;Fair Value Measurements,&#148; and SFAS No. 159, &#147;The Fair Value Option for
Financial Assets and Financial Liabilities.&#148;&#160;
Adoption of these Standards did not have a material impact on Abbott&#146;s
financial position.&#160; However, adoption of
SFAS No.159 and SFAS No. 157 resulted in a decrease to Earnings employed in the
business of approximately $189 million, substantially offset by an increase to
Accumulated other comprehensive income of approximately $182 million as of
January 1, 2007.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 22.5pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on Earnings</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Taxes on earnings reflect
the estimated annual effective rates and the effect of discrete tax events that
occurred in the second quarter of 2006.&#160; For
the six months ended June 30, 2006, 6.2 percentage points of tax benefit was
attributed to discrete items, primarily the tax benefit on acquired in-process
and collaborations research and development.&#160;
The effective tax rates are less than the statutory U.S. federal income
tax rate principally due to the domestic dividend exclusion and the benefit of
lower statutory tax rates and tax exemptions in several taxing jurisdictions.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .2pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Liquidity and
Capital Resources at June 30, 2007 Compared with December 31, 2006</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net cash from
operating activities for the first six months 2007 totaled approximately $2.6
billion.&#160; Abbott expects annual cash flow
from operating activities to continue to exceed Abbott&#146;s capital expenditures
and cash dividends.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At June 30, 2007
current assets exceeded current liabilities by approximately $329 million.&#160; At December 31, 2006 current liabilities
exceeded current assets by approximately $669 million as a result of increased
short-term borrowings used to acquire Kos Pharmaceuticals Inc. in December
2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .9pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At June 30, 2007,
Abbott&#146;s long-term debt rating was AA by Standard &amp; Poor&#146;s Corporation and
A1 by Moody&#146;s Investors Service.&#160; Abbott
has readily available financial resources, including unused lines of credit of
$7.0 billion<font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;">, </font>including
a $4.0 billion short-term facility, that support commercial paper borrowing
arrangements.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In October 2006, the
board of directors authorized the purchase of $2.5 billion of Abbott&#146;s common
shares from time to time and no shares were purchased under this authorization
in 2006.&#160; During the first six months of
2007, Abbott purchased approximately 15.4 million of its common shares at a
cost of approximately $827 million.&#160; In
the first six months of 2006, Abbott purchased approximately 17.3 million of
its common shares under a prior authorization at a cost of approximately $755
million.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .2pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under a
registration statement filed with the Securities and Exchange Commission in
February 2006, Abbott may offer and sell from time to time debt securities in
one or more offerings through February 2009.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Legislative Issues</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott&#146;s primary
markets are highly competitive and subject to substantial government regulation
throughout the world.&#160; Abbott expects
debate to continue over the availability, method of delivery, and payment for
health care products and services.&#160;
Abbott believes that if legislation is enacted, it could have the effect
of reducing access to health care products and services, or reducing prices or
the rate of price increases for health care products and services.&#160; It is not possible to predict the extent to
which Abbott or the health care industry in general might be adversely affected
by these factors in the future.&#160; A more
complete discussion of&nbsp;these factors is contained in Item 1, Business, and
Item 1A, Risk Factors on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended December 31, 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Private Securities
Litigation Reform Act of 1995 &#151; A Caution Concerning Forward-Looking Statements</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt .2pt 12.0pt 0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under the safe
harbor provisions of the Private Securities Litigation Reform Act of 1995,
Abbott cautions investors that any forward-looking statements or projections
made by Abbott, including those made in this document, are subject to risks and
uncertainties that may cause actual results to differ materially from those projected.
Economic, competitive, governmental, technological and other factors that may
affect Abbott&#146;s operations are discussed in Item 1A, Risk Factors to the Annual
Report on Form 10-K for the year ended December 31, 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin-left:0pt;margin-right:0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 4.</font></u><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">&#160;&#160;&#160; </font></b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Controls
and Procedures</font></u></p>

<p style="margin-left:36.0pt;margin-right:0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Evaluation of disclosure controls and procedures.&#160; </font></i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Chief Executive Officer, Miles D. White, and Chief Financial Officer, Thomas C.
Freyman, evaluated the effectiveness of Abbott Laboratories&#146; disclosure
controls and procedures as of the end of the period covered by this report, and
concluded that Abbott Laboratories&#146; disclosure controls and procedures were
effective to ensure that information Abbott is required to disclose in the
reports that it files or submits with the Securities and Exchange Commission
under the Securities Exchange Act of 1934 (the &#147;Exchange Act&#148;) is recorded,
processed, summarized and reported, within the time periods specified in the
Commission&#146;s rules and forms, and to ensure that information required to be
disclosed by Abbott in the reports that it files or submits under the Exchange
Act is accumulated and communicated to Abbott&#146;s management, including its
principal executive officer and principal financial officer, as appropriate to
allow timely decisions regarding required disclosure.</font></p>

<p style="margin-left:36.0pt;margin-right:0pt;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(b)</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-style:italic;">Changes in internal control over financial reporting.</font></i><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160; During the quarter ended June 30, 2007, there
were no changes in Abbott&#146;s internal control over financial reporting (as defined
in Rule 13a-15(f) under the Exchange Act) that have materially affected, or are
reasonably likely to materially affect, Abbott&#146;s internal control over
financial reporting.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">20</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<p style="margin-left:0pt;margin-right:0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PART II.&#160;&#160;&#160; OTHER INFORMATION</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 47.9pt;text-indent:-47.9pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 1.</font></u>
<font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; <u>Legal Proceedings</u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott is involved
in various claims, legal proceedings and investigations, including (as of June
30, 2007, except as otherwise indicated) those described below.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2006 Form
10-K, Abbott reported that six cases were pending in which Abbott seeks to
enforce its patents relating to divalproex sodium (a drug that Abbott sells
under the trademark Depakote&#174;).&#160;&#160; During
the quarter, Abbott filed three additional cases.&#160; Abbott seeks injunctive relief against the
following companies and their proposed generic versions of extended release
divalproex sodium:&#160; Teva Pharmaceuticals
USA, Inc. (filed May 2007 in the U.S. District Court for Delaware), Wockhardt
Limited and Wockhardt USA Inc. (filed May 2007 in the U.S. District Court for
New Jersey), and Impax Laboratories, Inc. (filed June 2007 in the U.S. District
Court for Delaware).</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its Form 10-Q
for the first quarter 2007, Abbott reported that two cases were pending in
which Abbott seeks to enforce a patent covering cefdinir (a drug that Abbott
sells in the United States under the trademark Omnicef&#174;).&#160; As previously disclosed, in one of those
cases, Abbott&#146;s motion for a preliminary injunction against two of the
defendants in that case, Sandoz and Teva, was denied.&#160; Abbott has appealed that denial of its motion
for a preliminary injunction.&#160; In <i>Lupin</i>, the court granted Lupin&#146;s motion
for summary judgment of non-infringement in part.&#160; Abbott has appealed the ruling on summary
judgment.&#160; At the request of the parties,
the court dismissed, without prejudice, the remainder of the parties&#146; claims
and counterclaims.&#160; The remaining
litigation related to cefdinir is not material to Abbott.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2006 Form
10-K, Abbott reported that a number of cases are pending that allege generally
that Abbott and numerous other pharmaceutical companies reported false pricing
information in connection with certain drugs that are reimbursable under
Medicare and Medicaid and by private payors.&#160;
As previously disclosed, the federal court cases have been consolidated
in the U.S. District Court for the District of Massachusetts as <i>In re: Pharmaceutical Industry Average Wholesale
Price Litigation, MDL 1456.</i>&#160;
In April 2007, Orange County, New York filed suit against Abbott and
numerous other manufacturers in the U.S. District Court in the Southern
District of New York, which was subsequently transferred to <i>MDL 1456</i>.&#160;
The previously reported case, <i>State
of Idaho</i>, was transferred to <i>MDL
1456</i>.&#160; Abbott previously
reported that it had filed with the MDL court a motion to dismiss the suit
brought by the Department of Justice.&#160; In
May 2007, the MDL court denied Abbott&#146;s motion to dismiss.&#160; While it is not feasible to predict with
certainty the outcome of the proceedings and investigations related to pricing
information for drugs reimbursable under Medicare and Medicaid, their ultimate
dispositions could be material to cash flows or results of operations for a
quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2006 Form
10-K, Abbott reported that the Office of the Inspector General of the United
States Department of Health and Human Services in conjunction with the United
States Department of Justice, through the United States Attorneys for the
Eastern District of Wisconsin </font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">21</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='21',FILE='C:\fc\21593955488_H11179_2307421\18715-1-di.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug  3 09:40 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">and the Western District of Louisiana, are
investigating the sales and marketing practices of Kos Pharmaceuticals, Inc., a
company Abbott acquired in December 2006.&#160;
During the quarter, Abbott was notified that the United States Attorney
for the Middle District of Louisiana is also investigating those practices.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2006 Form
10-K, Abbott reported that as of December 31, 2006, Abbott was a defendant in
numerous lawsuits involving the drug oxycodone (a drug sold under the trademark
OxyContin&#174;), which is manufactured by Purdue Pharma.&#160; Abbott previously promoted OxyContin under a
co-promotion agreement with Purdue Pharma.&#160;
Most of the lawsuits allege generally that plaintiffs suffered personal
injuries as a result of taking OxyContin. A few lawsuits allege consumer
protection violations and unfair trade practices. As of June 30, 2007, 28
lawsuits are pending in which Abbott is a party, all of which are individual
state court suits.&#160; Purdue Pharma is a
defendant in each lawsuit and, pursuant to the co-promotion agreement, Purdue
is required to indemnify Abbott in each lawsuit.&#160; The resolution of lawsuits by the other
parties has resulted in the decrease in lawsuits remaining against Abbott.<b>&#160; </b>Abbott
will no longer report on these cases.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In its 2006 Form
10-K, Abbott reported that a case is pending in the U.S. District Court for
Delaware against Medtronic, in which Abbott alleges that certain models of
Medtronic&#146;s stents infringe four of Abbott&#146;s Lau patents.&#160; As previously disclosed, a jury found that
Abbott&#146;s Lau patents were valid and infringed by all of the Medtronic stents in
question.&#160; In June 2007, Abbott filed a
motion seeking to enjoin Medtronic from using the infringing stent designs, and
Medtronic filed a motion to stay proceedings related to the injunction.&#160; Medtronic appealed to the Federal Circuit the
court&#146;s decision related to liability and inequitable conduct, and Abbott filed
a motion to dismiss that appeal as being premature.&#160; In August 2007, at Abbott&#146;s request, the
Federal Circuit dismissed Medtronic&#146;s appeal as premature.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In September 2006,
Abbott filed suit in the U.S. District Court for Delaware against Johnson &amp;
Johnson, Inc. (Johnson &amp; Johnson) and Cordis Corporation, a wholly owned
subsidiary of Johnson &amp; Johnson, requesting a declaratory judgment that
certain of Johnson &amp; Johnson&#146;s patents are invalid and/or that those
patents are not infringed by Abbott&#146;s Xience V stent.&#160; During 2007, additional patents were issued
to Johnson &amp; Johnson and Abbott amended its complaint to add those
additional patents and also filed a separate lawsuit on these patents seeking a
finding of non-infringement and invalidity.&#160;
During the second quarter, Cordis Corporation sued Abbott in the U.S.
District Court for New Jersey for infringement of these additional patents,
seeking an injunction, an award of damages and a determination of willful
infringement. Various motions are pending in the Delaware and New Jersey courts
seeking to determine the proper venue for these disputes.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">22</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='22',FILE='C:\fc\21593955488_H11179_2307421\18715-1-di.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug  3 09:40 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In July 2007,
Leonard Bronstein, an Abbott shareholder, filed a purported derivative lawsuit
in the U.S. District Court for the Northern District of Illinois on behalf of
Abbott against Abbott and each member of its Board of Directors (the
&#147;Defendants&#148;).&#160; The complaint alleges the
Defendants breached their fiduciary responsibilities in connection with
oversight of regulatory compliance with Food and Drug Administration
regulations which caused unspecified injury or damage to the Company.&#160; Plaintiff seeks an unspecified amount of
monetary damages for all losses Abbott suffered stemming from the alleged
breach of fiduciary duty.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While it is not
feasible to predict the outcome of such pending claims, proceedings and
investigations with certainty, management is of the opinion that their ultimate
dispositions should not have a material adverse effect on Abbott&#146;s financial
position, cash flows, or results of operations, except as noted above.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">23</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='23',FILE='C:\fc\21593955488_H11179_2307421\18715-1-di.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug  3 09:40 2007' -->

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0pt 0pt .0001pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><hr size="1" width="160" noshade color="black" align="left" style="width:120.0pt;"></div>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 72.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1.</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">These shares include:</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 108.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(i)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">the shares deemed surrendered to Abbott to pay the
exercise price in connection with the exercise of employee stock options &#151;
2,170,570 in April, 2,180,904 in May, and 419,348 in June; and</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 108.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(ii)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">the shares purchased on the open market for the
benefit of participants in the Abbott Canada Stock Retirement Plan &#151; 10,000 in
April, 10,000 in May, and 10,000 in June.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 72.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">These shares do
not include the shares surrendered to Abbott to satisfy tax withholding
obligations in connection with the vesting of restricted stock or restricted
stock units.</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 72.0pt;text-indent:-24.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2.</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On October 18, 2006, Abbott announced
that its board of directors approved the purchase of up to $2.5 billion of its
common shares.</font></p>


 <p style="margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">24</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='24',FILE='C:\fc\21593955488_H11179_2307421\18715-1-di.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug  3 09:40 2007' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">



<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 4.</font></u>&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; <u>Submission of Matters to a Vote of
Security Holders</u></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;text-indent:36.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Abbott Laboratories
held its Annual Meeting of Shareholders on April 27, 2007.&#160; The following is a summary of the matters
voted on at that meeting.</font></p>

<h5 style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:normal;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 36.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-18.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(a)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The shareholders elected
Abbott&#146;s entire Board of Directors.&#160; The
persons elected to Abbott&#146;s Board of Directors and the number of shares cast
for and the number of shares withheld, with respect to each of these persons,
were as follows:</h5>

of rental expense to be the amount representing return on capital, and (iii)

made, in light of the circumstances under which such statements were made, not
